✓ d. Pseudomonas aeruginosa

Explanation:
Malignant (necrotizing) otitis externa is an invasive infection most commonly caused by Pseudomonas aeruginosa, typically affecting elderly diabetics.

================================================================================
Question 551 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 30-year-old female presented with bilateral conductive hearing loss, which is gradual, progressive, and persistent. On examination, both tympanic membranes are intact. What is the most appropriate diagnosis?

Options:
✓ a. Otosclerosis
  b. Meniere's disease
  c. Presbycusis
  d. Chronic suppurative otitis media

Explanation:
Otosclerosis is a common cause of progressive bilateral conductive hearing loss in young to middle-aged adults, often with a normal tympanic membrane.

================================================================================
Question 552 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 45-year-old male patient presented to ENT OPD with vertigo, fluctuating hearing loss, tinnitus, and aural fullness. What is your most appropriate diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Otosclerosis
  b. Acute suppurative otitis media
  c. Serous otitis media
✓ d. Meniere's disease

Explanation:
The classic tetrad of symptoms for Meniere's disease includes episodic vertigo, fluctuating sensorineural hearing loss, tinnitus, and aural fullness.

================================================================================
Question 553 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 6-year-old child came to ENT OPD with bilateral decreased hearing, bilateral nasal obstruction, and snoring at night. What is your most appropriate diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Acute suppurative otitis media
  b. Chronic suppurative otitis media
✓ c. Serous otitis media
  d. Presbycusis

Explanation:
Adenoid hypertrophy causes nasal obstruction and snoring and frequently leads to Eustachian tube dysfunction, resulting in Serous Otitis Media (Otitis Media with Effusion) and hearing loss.

================================================================================
Question 554 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
In otosclerosis, on pure tone audiometry, there will be a Carhart notch at which frequency?

Options:
  a. 1000 Hz
✓ b. 2000 Hz
  c. 3000 Hz
  d. 4000 Hz

Explanation:
Carhart's notch is a dip in bone conduction thresholds at 2000 Hz (2 kHz) seen in otosclerosis.

================================================================================
Question 555 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 25-year-old male patient presented with vertigo which is sudden in onset and lasts for 20 to 30 seconds. Vertigo is position-related. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
✓ a. Benign paroxysmal positional vertigo
  b. Perilymph fistula
  c. Meniere's disease
  d. Vertebrobasilar insufficiency

Explanation:
Benign Paroxysmal Positional Vertigo (BPPV) is characterized by short episodes of vertigo (seconds) triggered by changes in head position.

================================================================================
Question 556 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 19-year-old female patient presented with right-sided facial palsy. On examination, there were vesicular rashes on the right pinna. What is the most definitive diagnosis?

Options:
✓ a. Herpes zoster
  b. Bell's palsy
  c. Neurofibroma
  d. Facial nerve tumor

Explanation:
Herpes Zoster Oticus (Ramsay Hunt syndrome) presents with facial nerve palsy and vesicular rash in the ear canal or pinna.

================================================================================
Question 557 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 20-year-old male patient presented with bilateral foul-smelling discharge which is scanty and purulent. What is the most appropriate diagnosis?

Options:
✓ a. Atticoantral disease
  b. Tubotympanic disease
  c. Serous otitis media
  d. Otitis externa

Explanation:
Scanty, foul-smelling purulent discharge is characteristic of unsafe CSOM (Atticoantral disease), often associated with cholesteatoma or bone erosion.

================================================================================
Question 558 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The pathogen responsible for localized otitis externa is:

Options:
✓ a. Staph aureus
  b. Strep pneumonia
  c. Klebsiella
  d. Proteus mirabilis

Explanation:
Localized otitis externa (furuncle) is an infection of the hair follicle, typically caused by Staphylococcus aureus.

================================================================================
Question 559 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 4-year-old child came to ENT emergency with sudden onset of dysphagia, fever, and stridor. On examination, the epiglottis is red and swollen. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Acute laryngitis
✓ b. Acute epiglottitis
  c. Acute laryngotracheobronchitis
  d. Chronic laryngitis

Explanation:
Acute epiglottitis is a medical emergency in children presenting with high fever, dysphagia, drooling, stridor, and a swollen 'cherry-red' epiglottis.

================================================================================
Question 560 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 40-year-old female patient came to ENT OPD with swelling in front of the right ear for the last 6 months, which is painless. On examination, the facial nerve is intact. What is your most probable diagnosis?

Options:
✓ a. Pleomorphic adenoma
  b. Mucoepidermoid carcinoma
  c. Acute parotitis
  d. Warthin's tumor

Explanation:
Pleomorphic adenoma is the most common benign tumor of the parotid gland, typically presenting as a slow-growing, painless swelling with an intact facial nerve.

================================================================================
Question 561 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 40-year-old female patient underwent parotid surgery 4 months back. Now she complains of sweating and flushing of the preauricular region. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
✓ a. Frey’s syndrome
  b. Hematoma
  c. Wound infection
  d. Injury to facial nerve

Explanation:
Frey's syndrome (gustatory sweating) is a complication of parotidectomy where autonomic nerve fibers cross-innervate, causing sweating in the preauricular skin during eating.

================================================================================
Question 562 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 60-year-old malnourished patient presents with regurgitation of undigested food at night. Gurgling sound is produced on swallowing. What is your most probable diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Achalasia
✓ b. Pharyngeal pouch
  c. Acute esophagitis
  d. Plummer-Vinson syndrome

Explanation:
A pharyngeal pouch (Zenker's diverticulum) causes regurgitation of undigested food, dysphagia, and a gurgling sound (borborygmi) in the neck.

================================================================================
Question 563 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Plummer-Vinson syndrome is a predisposing factor for:

Options:
  a. Esophageal tumors
✓ b. Hypopharyngeal tumors
  c. Pharyngeal pouch
  d. Achalasia

Explanation:
Plummer-Vinson syndrome increases the risk of developing post-cricoid carcinoma, which is a tumor of the hypopharynx.

================================================================================
Question 564 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50-year-old male patient presents with progressive unilateral sensorineural hearing loss. On examination, there is hypoaesthesia of the posterior meatal wall. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Noise-induced hearing loss
✓ b. Acoustic neuroma
  c. Meniere's disease
  d. Presbycusis

Explanation:
Unilateral progressive sensorineural hearing loss and Hitselberger's sign (hypoesthesia of the posterior meatal wall due to facial nerve compression) suggest Acoustic Neuroma (Vestibular Schwannoma).

================================================================================
Question 565 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 35-year-old male patient came to ENT OPD with chief complaints of episodic vertigo, fluctuating hearing loss, and tinnitus. On examination, both tympanic membranes are normal. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Otosclerosis
  b. Acute otitis media
✓ c. Meniere's disease
  d. CP angle tumors

Explanation:
The clinical picture describes the classic triad of Meniere's disease: episodic vertigo, fluctuating hearing loss, and tinnitus.

================================================================================
Question 566 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50-year-old male patient presents with right-sided neck swelling along with conductive deafness on the same side. He also has nasal obstruction. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Sinonasal tumors
✓ b. Nasopharyngeal carcinoma
  c. Deviated nasal septum
  d. Ethmoidal polyps

Explanation:
Trotter's triad for Nasopharyngeal Carcinoma includes conductive deafness (due to Eustachian tube blockage), ipsilateral temporoparietal neuralgia, and palatal paralysis. Neck swelling (node metastasis) and nasal obstruction are also common presentations.

================================================================================
Question 567 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
What is the most common benign sinonasal tumor?

Options:
  a. Hemangioma
✓ b. Inverted papilloma
  c. Lymphoma
  d. Malignant melanoma

Explanation:
Inverted papilloma is the most common and clinically significant benign epithelial tumor of the nose and paranasal sinuses. (Osteomas are also very common but among the options provided, Inverted Papilloma is the standard answer).

================================================================================
Question 568 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Rhinolith formation in the nasal cavity is due to deposition of:

Options:
✓ a. Calcium and magnesium salts
  b. Potassium
  c. Chloride
  d. Iron

Explanation:
Rhinoliths are formed by the deposition of insoluble salts of calcium and magnesium around a nidus in the nasal cavity.

Question 569 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A patient presents with intermittent swelling and pain in the upper part of the neck after eating, and it subsides after some time. There is no swelling in the oral cavity. What is your most probable diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Sialadenitis
✓ b. Submandibular duct stone
  c. Sjogren's syndrome
  d. Actinomycosis

Explanation:
Pain and swelling of a salivary gland associated with meals (Mealtime Syndrome) is characteristic of obstructive sialadenitis, commonly due to a submandibular duct stone.

Question 570 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 10-year-old boy presents in emergency to the ENT department with a history of sore throat and fever. On examination, there is a dirty grey membrane on both tonsils, which extends to the soft palate, and its removal causes bleeding. What could be your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Membranous tonsillitis
  b. Infectious mononucleosis
✓ c. Diphtheria
  d. Leukemia

Explanation:
A dirty grey, adherent membrane that bleeds on removal is the hallmark clinical finding of Diphtheria.

Question 571 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 4-year-old boy presents with a history of nasal trauma 24 hours ago. Now he has bilateral nasal obstruction. On examination, there is smooth swelling of the nasal septum which is fluctuant. How could you treat this patient?

Options:
  a. Incision and drainage
  b. Antibiotics
✓ c. Incision and drainage and antibiotics
  d. Analgesic

Explanation:
A septal hematoma (fluctuant septal swelling after trauma) requires immediate incision and drainage to prevent septal necrosis/abscess, followed by antibiotics.

Question 572 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 40-year-old male patient came with chief complaints of right-side nasal obstruction. On examination, there is a mass in the right nasal cavity. CT scan shows homogeneous opacity involving the right nasal cavity and maxillary sinus. If it is inverted papilloma, what will be the treatment of choice?

Options:
  a. Radiotherapy
  b. Chemotherapy
✓ c. Medial maxillectomy
  d. Intranasal polypectomy

Explanation:
Inverted papilloma requires complete surgical excision to prevent recurrence and malignant transformation. Medial maxillectomy (endoscopic or open) is the standard treatment.

A 40-year-old female patient presents with bilateral hearing loss. On examination, both tympanic membranes are normal. How will you investigate this patient?

  a. CT scan
  b. MRI
✓ c. PTA
  d. ERA

Explanation:
Pure Tone Audiometry (PTA) is the fundamental investigation for assessing the type and degree of hearing loss.

Question 574 (NMC - 2023)

Options:
  a. Tympanometry
✓ b. Electrocochleography
  c. Caloric test
  d. CT scan

Explanation:
Electrocochleography (ECochG) is the most specific electrophysiological test for diagnosing endolymphatic hydrops (Meniere's disease).

Question 575 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 40-year-old female patient comes to ENT OPD with a history of nasal discharge on bending forward for the last 10 days. The discharge is clear and watery. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Allergic rhinitis
✓ b. CSF rhinorrhea
  c. Acute sinusitis
  d. Atrophic rhinitis

Explanation:
Watery nasal discharge that increases with bending forward (reservoir sign) or straining is highly suggestive of Cerebrospinal Fluid (CSF) rhinorrhea.

Question 576 (NMC - 2023)

  a. Antrochoanal polyp
✓ b. Ethmoidal polyp
  c. Fungal sinusitis
  d. Malignant tumor

Explanation:
Bilateral, multiple, smooth, glistening masses in the nasal cavity are characteristic of ethmoidal polyps.

Question 577 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
An 8-year-old boy presented to ENT OPD with 3 days history of pain in the throat and high-grade fever. On examination, there is a whitish membrane over both tonsils. What is the most probable diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Diphtheria
✓ b. Acute membranous tonsillitis
  c. Oral candidiasis
  d. Infectious mononucleosis

Explanation:
High fever and pain with a whitish membrane suggest acute membranous tonsillitis. While Diphtheria is a differential, the acute high-fever presentation aligns well with acute non-diphtheritic infections or infectious mononucleosis (which can be termed membranous tonsillitis in broad classification).

Question 578 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50-year-old diabetic female patient had a history of severe pain in the right ear. On examination, there are granulation tissues in the external auditory meatus. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Acute otitis media
✓ b. Malignant otitis externa
  c. Secretory otitis media
  d. Furuncle

Explanation:
Severe ear pain in a diabetic with granulation tissue in the floor of the ear canal is the classic presentation of Malignant Otitis Externa.

================================================================================
Question 579 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 5-year-old child presents with decreased hearing and delayed speech for the last 3 months. She is diagnosed with otitis media with effusion. What will be the findings on tympanogram?

Options:
  a. Type A
✓ b. Type B
  c. Type AD
  d. Type AS

Explanation:
Otitis Media with Effusion (OME) typically produces a Type B (flat) tympanogram due to fluid in the middle ear restricting tympanic membrane movement.

================================================================================
Question 580 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50-year-old diabetic patient presents with right ear blockage and itching sensation. On autoscopic examination, there is a wet paper appearance in the external auditory meatus. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Diffuse otitis externa
✓ b. Otomycosis
  c. Furuncle
  d. Malignant otitis externa

Explanation:
Otomycosis (fungal ear infection) often presents with intense itching and a 'wet newspaper' appearance or visible fungal hyphae/spores.

Question 581 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 35-year-old school teacher presents with a change of voice for the last 2 months. He is a non-smoker and on indirect laryngoscopy, there is a polypoidal growth on the right vocal cord. What will be your treatment of choice in this patient?

Options:
  a. Cordectomy
  b. Speech therapy
✓ c. Direct laryngoscopy and excision
  d. Radiotherapy

Explanation:
Vocal cord polyps are surgically treated by microlaryngoscopic excision (Direct laryngoscopy and excision) followed by voice rest and therapy.

================================================================================
Question 582 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 30-year-old male patient presented with nasal blockage on and off for the last 1 month. On examination, there is nasal crusting and septal perforation. There is hematuria and deranged urea and creatinine. What is your most probable diagnosis?

Options:
  a. SLE
✓ b. Wegener's Granulomatosis
  c. Leishmaniasis
  d. Goodpasture syndrome

Explanation:
Wegener's Granulomatosis (Granulomatosis with Polyangiitis) involves the upper respiratory tract (crusting, perforation), lungs, and kidneys (glomerulonephritis/hematuria).

Question 583 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 3-year-old child presented with 3 days history of sudden onset of shortness of breath and cyanotic spells. On auscultation of the chest, there is decreased breath sound on the right side of the chest. The parents also give a history that the child was playing on the floor after which these symptoms developed. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Acute epiglottitis
  b. Acute laryngitis
✓ c. Foreign body in bronchial tree
  d. Acute bronchitis

Explanation:
Sudden onset of respiratory distress in a child with a history of playing on the floor suggests foreign body aspiration. Decreased breath sounds on one side indicate obstruction of a main bronchus.

================================================================================
Question 584 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 12-year-old girl presented to the ENT OPD with complaints of pain and swelling behind the right ear, having high-grade fever, toxic look, and lethargy. On examination, there is right side postauricular tenderness. Otoscopic findings show sagging of the posterior meatal wall. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Temporal abscess
  b. Bezold's abscess
✓ c. Acute mastoiditis
  d. Petrositis

Explanation:
Postauricular pain/swelling, fever, and sagging of the posterosuperior meatal wall are cardinal signs of acute mastoiditis.

================================================================================
Question 585 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50-year-old diabetic female patient presents with difficulty in swallowing for the last 10 days. On examination, there is ulceration over the buccal mucosa, soft palate, and uvula. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Diphtheria
  b. Aphthous ulcer
✓ c. Stomatitis
  d. Erythroplakia

Explanation:
Generalized inflammation and ulceration of the oral mucosa (buccal, palate, uvula) is termed stomatitis. In a diabetic, this could be infective (e.g., severe viral or candidal, though candidal is usually white patches). 'Aphthous' are usually discrete. Stomatitis is the broad descriptive diagnosis fitting the findings.

================================================================================
Question 586 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 45-year-old female patient presents with difficulty with liquid diet more than solid food and regurgitation of food particles at night time. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. GERD
  b. Scleroderma
✓ c. Cardiac achalasia
  d. Esophageal cancer

Explanation:
Achalasia typically presents with dysphagia to both solids and liquids (often liquids > solids initially or paradoxically) and regurgitation.

================================================================================
Question 587 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 40-year-old patient presents to your OPD with a history of sticking sensation and pooling of saliva. X-ray lateral view of the neck shows increased prevertebral shadow. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Esophageal cancer
  b. Laryngeal carcinoma
✓ c. Hypopharyngeal carcinoma
  d. Nasopharyngeal carcinoma

Explanation:
Pooling of saliva (Chevalier Jackson's sign) and widening of the prevertebral soft tissue shadow on X-ray suggest a mass in the hypopharynx or retropharyngeal space, such as hypopharyngeal carcinoma.

================================================================================
Question 588 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 3-year-old boy was brought to the ENT OPD by his father with complaints of foul-smelling discharge from the nose for the last 14 days. What is your probable diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Hemangioma
  b. Inverted papilloma
✓ c. Foreign body in the nose
  d. Schwannoma

Explanation:
Unilateral foul-smelling nasal discharge in a child is considered to be due to a foreign body until proven otherwise.

Question 589 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
What is the most specific treatment for peritonsillar abscess?

Options:
  a. IV antibiotics
  b. Tonsillectomy
✓ c. Incision and drainage of abscess along with antibiotics
  d. Analgesic

Explanation:
The definitive treatment for a peritonsillar abscess (Quinsy) is drainage (via incision or aspiration) combined with antibiotic therapy.

Question 590 (NMC - 2023)

Question:
A 55-year-old tubercular laryngitis patient presented with hoarseness of voice. In such a condition, which part of the larynx is mostly involved?

Options:
  a. Subglottic
  b. Anterior part of the larynx
  c. Glottis
✓ d. Posterior part of the larynx

Explanation:
Tuberculosis of the larynx typically affects the posterior part of the larynx (interarytenoid region, posterior vocal cords).

Question 591 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50-year-old banker presents to you in OPD with left-sided unilateral headache associated with lacrimation and discharge from the nose on the same side. CT scan of the paranasal sinuses is normal. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
✓ a. Cluster headache
  b. Migraine
  c. Sinusitis
  d. Temporal lobe abscess

Explanation:
Cluster headaches present as severe unilateral headache with ipsilateral autonomic symptoms (lacrimation, rhinorrhea, nasal congestion) and normal sinus imaging.

Question 592 (NMC - 2023)

Question:
A 9-year-old child presents to you with nasal obstruction and discharge for the last 2 years. On examination, there are crowded teeth and a high-arched palate. He is diagnosed with hypertrophied adenoids. Which investigation should be performed?

  a. U/S Neck
✓ b. X-ray lateral view of neck
  c. CBC
  d. X-ray neck AP view

Explanation:
X-ray lateral view of the nasopharynx (neck) is the standard simple imaging to assess adenoid size and airway patency.

Question 593 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 55-year-old chain smoker for the last 20 years presents to you in OPD with hoarseness of voice. On examination, there is cervical lymphadenopathy. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Hypopharyngeal carcinoma
✓ b. Laryngeal carcinoma
  c. Nasopharyngeal carcinoma
  d. Lung carcinoma

Explanation:
Persistent hoarseness in a smoker suggests laryngeal pathology. The presence of cervical lymphadenopathy indicates metastasis, consistent with laryngeal carcinoma.

================================================================================
Question 594 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 25-year-old patient presents to you with sore throat and difficulty in swallowing. On examination, there are granules on the posterior pharyngeal wall. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Acute tonsillitis
✓ b. Acute pharyngitis
  c. Oropharyngeal cancer
  d. Nasopharyngeal cancer

Explanation:
The presence of granules (prominent lymphoid follicles) on the posterior pharyngeal wall is often termed granular pharyngitis, which is a form of pharyngitis. In the context of options, 'Acute pharyngitis' is the closest fit for an inflammatory condition.

================================================================================
Question 595 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50-year-old patient presents to you with right-sided parotid swelling and facial paralysis for the last 3 months. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Pleomorphic adenoma
✓ b. Mucoepidermoid carcinoma
  c. Warthin tumor
  d. Squamous cell carcinoma of the neck

Explanation:
Facial nerve paralysis associated with a parotid mass is highly suggestive of malignancy. Mucoepidermoid carcinoma is the most common malignant parotid tumor.

================================================================================
Question 596 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 7-year-old child presents with foul-smelling ear discharge for the last 3 years. Now he is having high-grade fever, neck stiffness, and projectile vomiting. What is your diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Subdural abscess
  b. Lateral sinus thrombosis
✓ c. Meningitis
  d. Brain abscess

Explanation:
The triad of fever, neck stiffness (nuchal rigidity), and vomiting (signs of increased ICP) in a patient with CSOM indicates meningitis.

Question 597 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 15-year-old male patient with a history of bleeding from the nose on and off for the last 2 months. If he is a case of angiofibroma, which investigation should be done?

Options:
  a. U/S Neck
✓ b. CT scan of nose and PNS with contrast
  c. X-ray PNS
  d. Angiography

Explanation:
Contrast-enhanced CT scan is the primary diagnostic investigation for Juvenile Nasopharyngeal Angiofibroma to assess tumor extent and bony changes.

Question 598 (NMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 60-year-old diabetic patient presents with nasal obstruction on and off. On anterior rhinoscopy, there is blackish ulceration on the inferior turbinate. What is your most probable diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Angiofibroma
  b. Nasopharyngeal carcinoma
✓ c. Acute invasive fungal sinusitis
  d. Acute bacterial rhinosinusitis

Explanation:
Blackish ulceration (eschar) in the nose of a diabetic patient is the hallmark of acute invasive fungal sinusitis (mucormycosis).

Question 599 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 60 years old diabetic female presented with complaints of severe pain right ear, fever and serous discharge from right ear from the last 2 weeks. She is on oral hypoglycemics. Her blood investigations reveal poor glycemic control with HbA1C of 10%. Examination of right ear reveals a congested external canal with serous discharge and is very tender. This patient is suffering from

Options:
  a. Herpes Zooster Oticus
  b. Keratosis obturans
✓ c. Malignant otitis externa
  d. Otomycosis
  e. Osteoma

Explanation:
Malignant (necrotizing) otitis externa is a severe infection typically affecting elderly diabetic patients, characterized by severe pain, discharge, and granulation tissue in the ear canal, caused by Pseudomonas aeruginosa.

================================================================================
Question 600 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 2 years male old child presented with complaints of bilaterally decreased hearing since birth. Her parents report that he had neonatal jaundice at 10th day of life for which he required an exchange transfusion for his high bilirubin levels. Audiogram reveals he has 100dB of sensorineural hearing loss bilaterally. The option he has for auditory rehabilitation is:

Options:
  a. Brain stem implant
✓ b. Cochlear implant
  c. Hearing aid
  d. Non verbal cues
  e. Wait and watch policy

Explanation:
For profound sensorineural hearing loss (100dB) where hearing aids provide insufficient benefit, a cochlear implant is the standard option for auditory rehabilitation. Brain stem implants are reserved for cases with absent cochlear nerves.

================================================================================
Question 601 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 20-year-old patient presents with a feeling of pressure and fullness in both ears, particularly when traveling in an airplane. Examination reveals normal tympanic membranes. Which of the following conditions is the likely cause of these symptoms?

Options:
  a. Acute otitis media
✓ b. Eustachian tube dysfunction
  c. Serous otitis media
  d. Otitis externa
  e. Meniere’s disease

Explanation:
Difficulty equalizing middle ear pressure during altitude changes (airplane travel) with normal TM findings is characteristic of Eustachian tube dysfunction.

================================================================================
Question 602 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 30 years old female presented with complaints of painful left pinna after getting an ear piercing 6 days back. o/e , left pinna is swollen and is exquisitely tender with a fluctuant red swelling. The next step should be

Options:
  a. Antibiotics
  b. Conservative management
✓ c. Incision and drainage
  d. Heat pads
  e. Splintage of pinna

Explanation:
The presentation suggests a perichondrial abscess (fluctuant swelling) following piercing (perichondritis). The immediate management for an abscess is incision and drainage to prevent cartilage necrosis, along with antibiotics.

================================================================================
Question 603 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 65 years old male presented with complaints of decreased hearing left side along with tinnitus and vertigo from the last 4 years. O/E left tympanic membrane is normal. Tuning fork tests reveal Rinnie's positive in both ears with webers lateralizing towards the right ear. The interpretation of tuning fork tests is:

Options:
  a. Conductive deafness in left ear
  b. Conductive deafness in right ear
✓ c. Sensorineural deafness in left ear
  d. Sensorineural deafness in right ear
  e. Mixed hearing loss

Explanation:
Rinne positive implies Air Conduction > Bone Conduction (Normal or SNHL). Weber lateralizes to the better ear in SNHL. Lateralization to the right indicates the left ear is the affected ear with sensorineural hearing loss.

================================================================================
Question 604 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 34 years old male presented with complaints of left sided tinnitus, vertigo and aural fullness from the last 2 years. He also complains of decreased hearing in that ear. You are suspecting meniere's disease. the investigation which you will order to reach diagnosis in this case would be

Options:
  a. Audiogram
  b. Brain stem evoked response audiometry
✓ c. Electrocochleography
  d. MRI brain
  e. Otoacoustic emissions

Explanation:
Electrocochleography (ECochG) is a specific diagnostic test for Meniere's disease (endolymphatic hydrops), looking for an elevated SP/AP ratio.

Question 605 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 30-year-old female presents with recurrent episodes of transient vertigo. There is no history of hearing loss and tinnitus. Positional test (Dix Hallpike) results in nystagmus and vertigo. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Vestibular neuritis
  b. Meniere's disease
✓ c. Benign paroxysmal positional vertigo (BPPV)
  d. Acoustic neuroma
  e. Labyrinthitis

Explanation:
Recurrent transient vertigo triggered by position changes, with a positive Dix-Hallpike test and no hearing loss, is diagnostic of Benign Paroxysmal Positional Vertigo (BPPV).

Question 606 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 24 years old female presented with complaints of chronically discharging ears from the last 4 years. She has taken multiple antibiotics with no improvement. Examination of the ears reveal bilateral perforations with active discharge in both ears. Her CT scan shows hazy mastoids. The next investigation in this patient which will help in management is:

Options:
  a. Audiogram
  b. Examination under a microscope
  c. Full blood profile
✓ d. Pus for culture and sensitivity
  e. MRI brain

Explanation:
In chronic otitis media with active discharge that is resistant to multiple antibiotics, obtaining a pus swab for culture and sensitivity is crucial to identify the causative organism and select appropriate antibiotics.

Question 607 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 30-year-old female presents with recurrent episodes of severe vertigo associated with hearing loss and tinnitus. Patient suddenly falls on the ground without loss of consciousness. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Vestibular neuritis
✓ b. Meniere's disease
  c. Benign paroxysmal positional vertigo (BPPV)
  d. Acoustic neuroma
  e. Labyrinthitis

Explanation:
The triad of vertigo, hearing loss, and tinnitus indicates Meniere's disease. Sudden falls without loss of consciousness (Tumarkin's otolithic crisis or Drop attacks) are a known complication of Meniere's.

Question:
A 40-year-old patient complains of gradual hearing loss in both ears, especially for high-pitched sounds. There is a history of prolonged exposure to loud noise at the workplace. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  a. Presbycusis
  b. Meniere's disease
  c. Otitis externa
  d. Conductive hearing loss
✓ e. Noise induced hearing loss

Explanation:
History of prolonged noise exposure and high-frequency hearing loss is characteristic of Noise-Induced Hearing Loss (NIHL).

Options:
✓ a. Acute otitis media
  b. Chronic otitis media
  c. Otitis externa
  d. Serous otitis media

Question 610 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 40 years old male presented with complaints of right sided tinnitus and vertigo from the last 5 years. he has taken multiple medications for it but with no improvement. Rather his symptoms have worsened over time. O/E right TM is normal. Tuning fork tests are also normal. The next investigation in this patient would be

Options:
  a. Audiogram
  b. Brain stem evoked response audiometry
  c. Electrocochleography
✓ d. MRI brain
  e. Speech discrimination score

Explanation:
Unilateral tinnitus and vertigo warrant investigation for retrocochlear pathology, such as a vestibular schwannoma (acoustic neuroma). MRI of the brain/IAM is the gold standard for diagnosis.

Question 611 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50-year-old patient presents with recurrent episodes of severe pain and swelling below the jaw, especially during meals. On palpation, you feel a tender, fluctuant mass. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
✓ a. Submandibular sialadenitis
  b. Parotitis
  c. Sublingual gland abscess
  d. Pharyngitis
  e. Ludwig’s angina

Explanation:
Pain and swelling below the jaw (submandibular region) exacerbated by meals (mealtime syndrome) is classic for obstructive sialadenitis, likely due to a stone (sialolithiasis) in the submandibular gland.

Question 612 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 25-year-old patient presents with a complaint of a scratchy and painful throat, along with mild fever. On examination, you notice redness and swelling in the back of the throat, as well as white patches on the tonsils. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
✓ a. Infectious mononucleosis
  b. Viral pharyngitis
  c. Granular tonsillitis
  d. Laryngitis
  e. Acute glossitis

Explanation:
White patches (exudate) on the tonsils with sore throat and fever can indicate bacterial tonsillitis or Infectious Mononucleosis. Among the options provided, Infectious Mononucleosis fits the description of exudative tonsillitis.

Question 613 (NWSM - 2023)

Question:
A 17-year-old patient visits your clinic with complaints of a persistent sore throat, mild fever and discomfort in the abdomen. Physical examination reveals swollen tonsils with scrapable white patches and palpable cervical lymph nodes. The patient's fatigue seems disproportionate to the symptoms. What condition should be considered in this case?

Options:
  a. Common Cold
  b. Gastroenteritis
  c. Diphtheria
✓ d. Infectious mononucleosis
  e. Streptococcal tonsillitis

Explanation:
The combination of sore throat, tonsillar exudates, cervical lymphadenopathy, significant fatigue, and abdominal discomfort (likely splenomegaly) is classic for Infectious Mononucleosis.

Question 617 (NWSM - 2023)

Question:

Options:
  a. Empiric antibiotic therapy

  c. Chest X-ray to evaluate for metastasis
✓ d. Biopsy of the lesion
  e. High-dose corticosteroid therapy

Question 618 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 40 years old man presents with watering and photophobia in his left. He gives history of trauma to his left upper eyelid due to road traffic accident. On examination the left upper eyelid skin is shortened and scarred leading to lagophthalmos. He has exposure keratitis and conjunctivitis. The most likely diagnosis is; OPTION LIST

Options:
✓ Cicatricial ectropion
  Congenital ectropion.
  Mechanical ectropion.
  Paralytic (facial nerve palsy) ectropion.
  Senile (involutional) ectropion

Explanation:
The history of trauma leading to scarring and shortening of the left upper eyelid skin, resulting in lagophthalmos (inability to close the eyelid) and subsequent exposure keratitis and conjunctivitis, is characteristic of cicatricial ectropion. This type of ectropion is caused by the contraction of scar tissue on the eyelid.

================================================================================
Question 619 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 70 years old man presents to eye OPD with the complaints of watering from his right eye. On examination the right lower eyelid is everted but the skin is not scarred or shortened. There is chronic conjunctivitis and exposure keratitis. The most likely diagnosis is

Options:
  Cicatricial ectropion.
  Congenital ectropion.
  Mechanical ectropion.
  Paralytic (facial nerve palsy) ectropion.
✓ Senile (involutional) ectropion.

Explanation:
In an elderly patient, eversion of the lower eyelid (ectropion) without scarring or shortening of the skin, leading to watering, chronic conjunctivitis, and exposure keratitis, is most commonly caused by senile (involutional) ectropion. This occurs due to age-related horizontal laxity of the eyelid and weakening of the orbicularis oculi muscle.

================================================================================
Question 620 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50 years old lady presents to eye O.P.D with the complaint of watering and burning sensation in her Rt. Eye. On examination the patient has Rt. Lagophthalmos and exposure keratitis. Her mouth is deviated to the left side and is unable to lift her Rt.eyebrow. The eyelid skin is normal. The most likely diagnosis;

Options:
  Cicatricial ectropion.
  Congenital ectropion
  Mechanical ectropion.
✓ Paralytic (facial nerve palsy) ectropion
  Senile (involutional) ectropion

Explanation:
The presence of right lagophthalmos (inability to close the eyelid), exposure keratitis, mouth deviation to the left, and inability to lift the right eyebrow are all signs of right facial nerve (VII) palsy. Weakness of the orbicularis oculi muscle due to facial nerve palsy leads to paralytic ectropion, where the lower eyelid sags and turns outward.

Question 621 (NWSM - 2023)

Question:
A 12-years old girl is brought by her parents to Ophthalmology OPD. According to the parents, the patient has congenital cataracts since birth. What is the most important complication of untreated congenital cataracts?

Options:
  Retinal detachment
  Corneal ulcer
✓ Amblyopia
  Optic disc atrophy
  Lens subluxation

Explanation:
The most significant consequence of unoperated congenital cataract is stimulus-deprivation Amblyopia.

Question 622 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 25 years old male presented with complaints of right ear pain and decreased hearing from the last 2 days. According to the patient, his symptoms started after coming back from swimming in a local pond. O/E external auditory canal appears red and congested. Organism responsible for this condition is:

Options:
✓ E.coli
  hemophilus influenza
  mozarella catarrhalis (Moraxella)
  streptococcus pneumoniae
  Yersinia pestis

Explanation:
The clinical presentation describes Otitis Externa (Swimmer's Ear). While Pseudomonas aeruginosa is the most common causative organism, it is not listed in the options. Among the choices provided, E. coli (a gram-negative bacterium found in contaminated water sources like ponds) is the most plausible pathogen for an external canal infection acquired from swimming.

Question 623 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 40 years old female was involved in a road traffic accident. She received trauma to the left temporal bone. When she was examined, she had intact hearing but had decreased lacrimation left eye. The nerve involved is:

Options:
  chorda tympani nerve
  facial nerve branch to posterior belly of digastric
✓ greater superficial petrosal nerve
  nerve to stapedius
  tympanic plexus

Explanation:
The Greater Superficial Petrosal Nerve (GSPN) is a branch of the facial nerve that arises from the geniculate ganglion and carries parasympathetic fibers to the lacrimal gland. Injury to the GSPN (often in longitudinal temporal bone fractures) results in decreased lacrimation (Schirmer's test would be positive) while sparing hearing if the cochlea is intact.

Question 624 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 60 years old diabetic female presented with complaints of severe pain right ear, fever and serous discharge from right ear from the last 2 weeks. She is on oral hypoglycemics. Her blood investigations reveal poor glycemic control With HbA1C Of 10%. Examination Of right ear reveals a congested external canal With serous discharge and is very tender. This patient is suffering from:

Options:
  Herpes Zooster Oticus
  keratosis obturans
✓ malignant otitis externa
  Otomycosis
  osteoma

Explanation:
Malignant (Necrotizing) Otitis Externa is an aggressive infection of the external ear canal that spreads to the skull base, classically occurring in elderly diabetics with poor glucose control. Key features include severe otalgia (often out of proportion to exam), otorrhoea, and granulation tissue.

Question 625 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 30-year-old female presents with recurrent episodes of severe vertigo associated with hearing loss and tinnitus. Patient suddenly falls on the ground without loss of consciousness. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Vestibular neuritis
✓ Meniere's disease
  Benign paroxysmal positional vertigo (BPPV)
  Acoustic neuroma
  Labyrinthitis

Explanation:
This patient presents with the classic triad of Meniere's disease: episodic vertigo, fluctuating sensorineural hearing loss, and tinnitus. The sudden falls without loss of consciousness are known as Tumarkin's otolithic crisis (drop attacks), which can occur in Meniere's disease.

Question 626 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 4 years old female child presented with complaints of delayed speech and decreased hearing since childhood. O/E both tympanic membranes looked normal. She was investigated and found to have a sensorineural hearing loss of 95db. She was put in the cochlear implant surgery program. Before embarking on surgery, which investigation should be ordered:

Options:
  Brain stem evoked response audiometry
  CT scan to rule out inner ear anomalies
  Midbrain evoked potentials
✓ MRI to rule out brain pathology
  PET scan for viable audiologic pathways

Explanation:
While CT scans are used to assess bony anatomy, MRI is the gold standard pre-operative investigation for cochlear implants to assess the patency of the cochlea (fluid status) and, crucially, to confirm the presence and integrity of the vestibulocochlear nerve (CN VIII), ensuring it is not aplastic.

Question 627 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 30 years old male with involved in a road traffic accident. He presented to ER with a concussion and a fractured nose. He is managed conservatively and is making good progress after being shifted to ward. The next day, the surgeon on call receives a call from the ward that the patient has clear fluid coming out from nose, particularly on bending forward and is unable to sniff it back. The investigation to be done in this case is:

Options:
✓ B2 transferrin
  CSF analysis
  serum aldosterone levels
  MRI brain
  urinary catecholamines

Explanation:
The clinical picture suggests CSF Rhinorrhea (CSF leak) following head trauma, indicated by the 'reservoir sign' (fluid dripping on bending forward). The most specific test to confirm the fluid is Cerebrospinal Fluid is the detection of Beta-2 Transferrin, a protein found almost exclusively in CSF.

Question 628 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 14 years old adolescent boy presented with complaints of brisk epistaxis from the last 6 months. According to him, the bleeding is so severe that he required a blood transfusion on one instance. O/E, patient had a polypoidal growth right side nasal cavity. The next step in management of this patient would be:

Options:
  Arrange for nasal endoscopy
  Manage conservatively
✓ Order a CT scan
  Request coagulation profile
  Shift for surgery

Explanation:
The presentation of an adolescent male with a nasal mass and severe, recurrent epistaxis is highly suggestive of Juvenile Nasopharyngeal Angiofibroma (JNA). Biopsy is contraindicated due to the risk of torrential hemorrhage. The next appropriate step is a CT scan (with contrast) to define the extent of the tumor before planning treatment.

Question 629 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 20-year-old patient presents with a feeling of pressure and fullness in both ears, particularly when traveling in an airplane. Examination reveals normal tympanic membranes. Which of the following conditions is the likely cause of these symptoms?

Options:
  Acute otitis media
✓ Eustachian tube dysfunction
  Serous otitis media
  Otitis externa
  Meniere's disease

Explanation:
Pain and fullness in the ears during changes in atmospheric pressure (like air travel) with a normal otoscopic exam is characteristic of Eustachian Tube Dysfunction (Barotrauma).

Question 630 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 25 years old female presented with complaints of bilaterally decreased hearing from the last 9 years. According to the patient, she had bilateral ear discharge since childhood but has now dry ears from the last 12 months. O/E there are dry perforations with no discharge in both ears. The best option for auditory rehabilitation in this patient is:

Options:
  brain stem devices
  cochlear implant
  conservative treatment
  hearing aid
✓ myringoplasty

Explanation:
The patient has Chronic Otitis Media (Mucosal/Inactive) with a dry central perforation. Since the ear has been dry for a sufficient period (12 months), the best management for auditory rehabilitation and to seal the middle ear is surgical repair of the tympanic membrane, known as Myringoplasty.

Question 631 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 60 years old diabetic female with active covid infection presented with complaints of left facial swelling and decreased vision left eye from the last 7 days. O/E there is diffuse erythema left side face and extensive black eschar is seen in nose. The patient also has complete ophthalmoplegia left eye and necrotic patch on hard palate. The clinical diagnosis in this case is:

Options:
  Chronic rhinosinusitis
  Inverted papilloma
✓ Mucormycosis
  Sarcoidosis
  Sinonasal malignancy

Explanation:
The combination of diabetes, COVID-19 (immunosuppression/steroid use), black eschar in the nose/palate, and rapid orbital involvement (ophthalmoplegia) is the classic presentation of Rhino-orbital-cerebral Mucormycosis (Black Fungus).

Question 632 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 10 years old female presented with recurrent attacks of nasal polyposis and chest infections from the last 5 years. Despite aggressive treatment strategies, her polyps recur and her chest infections also are getting worse. Her sweat chloride test was ordered and it was abnormal. The child is suffering from:

Options:
  allergic rhinitis
  chronic rhinosinusitis
✓ Cystic fibrosis
  Rhinolith
  sarcoidosis

Explanation:
Nasal polyposis in a child is rare and should raise suspicion for Cystic Fibrosis. The combination of recurrent polyps, chronic chest infections, and a positive sweat chloride test confirms the diagnosis of Cystic Fibrosis.

Question 633 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
43 years old male patient came through OPD with the history of nasal obstruction, headache, post nasal drip associated with decreased sense of smell, lethargy and intermittent ear. On examination of the nose there is white glistening soft tissue mass which are insensitive to touch. Which is the most suitable option of the following:

Options:
  Acute rhinosinusitis with nasal polyposis
  Allergic rhinosinusitis
  Acute invasive fungal rhinosinusitis
✓ Chronic rhinosinusitis with nasal polyposis
  Chronic invasive fungal rhinosinusitis

Explanation:
Pale, glistening, insensate masses in the nasal cavity are characteristic of nasal polyps. The chronicity of symptoms (obstruction, anosmia, post-nasal drip) points to Chronic Rhinosinusitis with Nasal Polyposis (CRSwNP).

Question 634 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 55-year-old male smoker presents with hoarseness and a progressively worsening cough. He also complains of difficulty swallowing. Laryngoscopy reveals a lesion involving the right vocal cord with irregular borders and areas of ulceration. What is the most appropriate next step?

Options:
  Empiric antibiotic therapy
  Immediate surgical excision
  Chest X-ray to evaluate for metastasis
✓ Biopsy of the lesion
  High-dose corticosteroid therapy

Explanation:
A suspicious, ulcerated laryngeal lesion in a smoker strongly suggests malignancy (Squamous Cell Carcinoma). The definitive next step to establish the diagnosis is a direct laryngoscopy and biopsy of the lesion.

Question 635 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 10 year old boy came to ENT OPD with right ear pain and discharge since 4 days. There was a previous episode of a common cold. Examination shows small central perforation. The most effective treatment would be:

Options:
  cortical mastoidectomy
  Myringotomy
✓ Starting medical treatment
  using lignocaine drops to relieve pain
  wait for spontaneous improvement

Explanation:
This is a case of Acute Otitis Media (AOM) that has perforated (AOM with perforation). The most effective treatment is medical management, typically involving oral antibiotics and topical aural toilet to clear the discharge.

Question 636 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 40 years old male presented with complaints of decreased hearing right side and fever. According to the patient, the fever is episodic and mostly comes at night with shivering. O/E there is extensive cholesteatoma in right ear. CT reveals erosion of tegmen plate and right sigmoid sinus thrombosis. The management option for this patient is:

Options:
  Atticotomy
  Broad spectrum antibiotics
  conservative management
✓ modified radical mastoidectomy
  tympanoplasty

Explanation:
The patient has unsafe chronic otitis media (cholesteatoma) complicated by Sigmoid Sinus Thrombosis (indicated by the 'picket fence' fever and CT findings). The definitive treatment is surgery to remove the disease and address the complications, which is a Modified Radical Mastoidectomy (or Canal Wall Down mastoidectomy).

Question 637 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
60 years old male patient who is known case of uncontrolled diabetes and hypertension admitted in medical ward for fever, progressively increasing headache and has developed left periorbital edema for the last one day. On examination there is black crusting in his left nasal cavity and has restricted eye movements with decreased visual acuity. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Allergic Rhinosinusitis
  Acute bacterial rhinosinusitis
  Acute meningitis
  Chronic fungal rhinosinusitis
✓ Mucormycosis

Explanation:
Black crusting (eschar) in the nasal cavity in an uncontrolled diabetic with orbital symptoms (edema, ophthalmoplegia, vision loss) is the hallmark of invasive fungal rhinosinusitis, specifically Mucormycosis.

Question 638 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
Nine years old child brought by her mother to Otolaryngology clinic giving history of behavioural changes like watching TV with loud sound and doesnt respond to a slow voice calling him from behind for the last 8-10 months. Her hearing was satisfactory before that. On otoscopy, both the tympanic membranes are retracted, dull looking appearance and there is no tenderness on palpation. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Acute otitis media
  Chronic otitis media
  Chronic mastoiditis
✓ Otitis media with effusion
  Otitis externa

Explanation:
Otitis Media with Effusion (OME), also known as Glue Ear, is common in children and presents with painless conductive hearing loss (turning up TV volume). The otoscopic appearance of a dull, retracted TM is typical.

Question 640 (NWSM - 2025)

Question:
A 10 year old boy came to ENT OPD with complain of right ear sever pain and fever followed by cold and flu. He has no previous such history. On otoscopic examination right tympanic membrane is red, congested with loss of light reflex. The most likely cause would be:

Options:
  otitis externa

Question 641 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 65 years old male presented with complaints of decreased hearing both ears from the last 5 years. According to the patient, he has worked in a factory for 25 years with moderate levels of noise exposure. he is non diabetic and non hypertensive. Both his tympanic membranes are normal with tuning fork tests showing sensorineural hearing loss. Finding you would expect on audiogram of this patient would be:

Options:
  Airbone gap
  Carharts notch
✓ Dip in bone conduction at 4kHz
  Low frequency SNHL
  Rising type curve on PTA

Explanation:
Noise-Induced Hearing Loss (NIHL) typically presents as a sensorineural hearing loss with a characteristic 'notch' or dip in hearing thresholds at 4000 Hz (4kHz) on the audiogram.

Question 642 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 30 years old male presented with a depressed nasal dorsum from the last 3 years. According to him, his deformity gradually worsened With time. O/E, there is a septal perforation With crusting and a saddle nose. Upon further enquiry, the patient also had red cell casts in urine and decreased renal function. Blood tests were ordered and his C-ANCA came out to be positive. The patient is suffering from:

Options:
  Buergers disease
  sarcoidosis
  syphilis
  tuberculosis
✓ Wegeners granulomatosis

Explanation:
The triad of upper respiratory tract involvement (saddle nose, crusting, perforation), renal involvement (red cell casts/glomerulonephritis), and positive c-ANCA is diagnostic for Granulomatosis with Polyangiitis (formerly Wegener's Granulomatosis).

Question 643 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 14-year-old boy presents with a history of foul-smelling, scanty, persistent ear discharge from the right ear for the past 6 months, associated With progressive hearing loss. He denies ear pain or fever. On otoscopic examination, there is a marginal perforation in the posterosuperior quadrant of the tympanic membrane with crusts and pearly white flakes visible in the middle ear. The posterior canal wall appears eroded.

Options:
  Chronic otitis media - mucosal type
  Otitis externa
  Tympanosclerosis
✓ Cholesteatoma
  Otitis media with effusion

Explanation:
A marginal perforation in the attic or posterosuperior quadrant with foul-smelling discharge and pearly white flakes is the hallmark description of Squamosal Chronic Otitis Media, also known as Cholesteatoma.

Question 644 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 30 years old male patient came through OPD with the history of otalgia due to which he couldn't sleep last night. He also gives history of ear picking. On examination the pinna is tender. What is the most probable diagnosis:

Options:
  Acute otitis media
  Acute mastoiditis
✓ Acute otitis externa
  Acute parotitis
  Acute Rhinosinusitis

Explanation:
Severe otalgia, history of trauma (ear picking), and specifically tenderness on manipulation of the pinna or tragus are characteristic of Acute Otitis Externa.

Question 645 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
What would be the appropriate management of a 5 year old child presenting with right foul smelling ear discharge, fever and otalgia. On examination his right pinna is pushed forward.

Options:
  Topical Antibiotic drops
  Topical steroid drops
  Oral antibiotics
✓ IV antibiotics with or without cortical mastoidectomy
  Watch and wait

Explanation:
A child with AOM presenting with pinna displacement (pushed forward) suggests Acute Mastoiditis. This requires admission and IV antibiotics. If a subperiosteal abscess is present or there is no improvement, a Cortical Mastoidectomy is indicated.

Question 646 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 40 years old male with uncontrolled diabetes presents with left sided facial pain and swelling from the last 6 days. O/E he had fungal debris occupying left maxillary sinus and left ethmoids. It has breached the left lamina papyracae but has not yet involved the orbit He is diagnosed as having acute fulminant fungal rhinosinusitis. The key to achieving disease control in this case is:

Options:
  anti fungals
  IV antibiotics
  good renal function
  hyperbaric Oxygen
✓ strict glucose control

Explanation:
In Mucormycosis (Acute Fulminant Fungal Rhinosinusitis), while surgical debridement and Amphotericin B are essential, the underlying metabolic acidosis and hyperglycemia (DKA) allow the fungus to thrive. Strict glucose control and reversal of ketoacidosis are the key systemic factors to stop the fungal proliferation.

================================================================================
Question 647 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 4 years old male presented with fever and right ear pain from the last 5 days. According to the patient's mother, he had severe pain in the right ear but his condition improved when she observed yellowish foul smelling discharge in his right ear. Culture of this discharge will likely yield which pathogen:

Options:
  bacteroides fragilis
  Clostridium difficile
  E. coli
  Moxarella Catarrhalis
✓ Streptococcus Pneumoniae

Explanation:
This is a classic presentation of Acute Otitis Media with spontaneous perforation (pain relief upon discharge). The most common causative organism for AOM is Streptococcus pneumoniae.

Question 648 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 35 years old male with nasal polyposis and seasonal allergic rhinitis is evaluated in clinic. Upon enquiry, he is found to be allergic to aspirin too. You are suspecting that this patient has samter's triad. What other pathology would you expect in this patient as a part of this triad:

Options:
  Anosmia
✓ Bronchial asthma
  dextrocardia
  infertility
  sensorineaural hearing loss

Explanation:
Samter's Triad (also known as Aspirin Exacerbated Respiratory Disease - AERD) consists of: 1. Aspirin sensitivity, 2. Nasal Polyps, and 3. Bronchial Asthma.

Question 649 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 20-year-old presents to the emergency department with fever and left eye proptosis for 3 days. On examination, he has restricted ocular movements and decreased vision. He is diagnosed with orbital cellulitis. Considering the most common source of infection spreading to the orbit, what is the most likely origin?

Options:
  Dacryocystitis
  Dental infection
  Endogenous (hematogenous) spread
✓ Paranasal sinuses (sinusitis)
  Acute hordeolum

Explanation:
The most common source of Orbital Cellulitis is the direct extension of infection from the paranasal sinuses, most frequently the ethmoid sinuses.

Question 650 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Rinne’s test positive means that.

Options:
✓ Air conduction is better than bone conduction
  Bone conduction is better than air conduction
  Bone is equal to air conduction
  Cholesteatoma
  Otosclerosis

Explanation:
Rinne's test compares air conduction (AC) to bone conduction (BC). A positive Rinne's test indicates that air conduction is heard louder and longer than bone conduction (AC > BC), which is either normal hearing or sensorineural hearing loss.

================================================================================
Question 651 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Greisinger’s sign means:

Options:
  Pain over the tempromandibular joint
  Pain in the eye
✓ Pain and tenderness over the mastoid
  Pain and tenderness over the auricle
  Acute suppurative otitis media

Explanation:
Griesinger's sign is characterized by edema, pain, and tenderness over the mastoid process, caused by thrombophlebitis of the mastoid emissary vein, often seen in lateral sinus thrombosis (a complication of otitis media).

Question 652 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Tonsillar artery is a branch from.

Options:
  Lingual artery
  Maxillary artery
✓ Facial artery
  Occipital artery
  Interna caretoid artery

Explanation:
The tonsillar artery, which is the main arterial supply to the palatine tonsils, is a branch of the facial artery.

Question 653 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Bulla ethmoidalis is present in:

Options:
  Inferior nasal meatus
✓ Middle nasal meatus
  Superior nasal meatus
  Nasopharynx
  Ethmoid sinus

Explanation:
The bulla ethmoidalis is an anatomical landmark located in the middle nasal meatus. It is the largest and most constant anterior ethmoid air cell.

================================================================================
Question 654 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Retracted drum is characterized by all the following except:

Options:
  Disturbed cone of light
  Prominent malleolar folds
  Decreased drum mobility
✓ Central drum perforation
  Conductive deafness

Explanation:
A retracted tympanic membrane (drum) is characterized by a disturbed cone of light, prominent malleolar folds, and decreased mobility due to negative pressure in the middle ear, leading to conductive deafness. A central drum perforation is a *cause* of conductive deafness, but it's a hole in the drum, not a characteristic of retraction itself.

================================================================================
Question 655 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The best treatment of otosclerosis:

Options:
  Grommet’s tube
✓ Stapedectomy
  Myringoplasty
  Mastoidectomy
  Adenoidectomy

Explanation:
Stapedectomy (or stapedotomy) is the surgical treatment of choice for otosclerosis. It involves removing the fixed stapes footplate and replacing it with a prosthesis to restore sound conduction.

================================================================================
Question 656 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Early glottic carcinoma is best treated by:

Options:
✓ Radiotherapy
  Total laryngectomy
  Antibiotics
  Cryosurgery
  Anticancerous therapy

Explanation:
Early glottic carcinoma (T1a) is best treated by either radiotherapy or endoscopic laser resection (cordectomy). Radiotherapy offers excellent cure rates with good voice preservation.

================================================================================
Question 657 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
On tracheostomy, apnea developed after incising the trachea is due to:

Options:
  Sudden wash of CO2 in the trachea
✓ Sudden release of the pressure in trachea
  Reflex vagal stimulation
  None of the above
  Sudden wash of O2

Explanation:
Apnea (temporary cessation of breathing) immediately after incising the trachea during tracheostomy for chronic upper airway obstruction is often due to the sudden relief of obstruction. This leads to a rapid washout of accumulated CO2, removing the primary respiratory drive and resulting in temporary apnea until the respiratory centers readjust.

Question 658 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The most common cause of esophageal stricture in children is:

Options:
  Esophageal carcinoma
  Diphtheria
  Achalasia of the cardia
✓ Corrosive intake
  Endoscopy

Explanation:
In children, the most common cause of esophageal stricture (narrowing of the esophagus) is the accidental ingestion of corrosive substances (e.g., strong acids or alkalis found in household cleaners), leading to chemical burns and subsequent scar formation.

Question 659 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
Juvenile nasopharyngeal angiofibroma is characterized by the following except:

Options:
  Affects teenagers
  Causes nasal obstructions
  Very vascular tumor
✓ Affects only females
  Profuse epistaxis

Explanation:
Juvenile nasopharyngeal angiofibroma (JNA) is a highly vascular tumor that almost exclusively affects adolescent males, causing symptoms like nasal obstruction and recurrent, profuse epistaxis. It does not affect only females.

Question 660 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
Fossa of Rosenmullar is a common site for:

Options:
  Angiofibroma
  Lipoma
  Adenoid
✓ Nasopharyngeal carcinoma
  Pharyngeal pouch

Explanation:
The Fossa of Rosenmüller (pharyngeal recess) in the lateral wall of the nasopharynx is the most common site of origin for nasopharyngeal carcinoma (NPC).
