Question 661 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Nasopharyngeal carcinoma early sign of nasopharyngeal carcinoma is:

Options:
✓ Unilateral secretory otitis media
  Trotter’s triad
  Petrositis
  Nasal obstruction
  Epistaxis

Explanation:
One of the earliest and most common presenting signs of nasopharyngeal carcinoma (NPC) is unilateral secretory otitis media. This occurs due to obstruction of the ipsilateral Eustachian tube by the tumor, leading to middle ear effusion and conductive hearing loss.

================================================================================
Question 662 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Stridor means:

Options:
  Difficult expiration
✓ Difficult inspiration
  Both
  Dysphagia
  Dysphagia

Explanation:
Stridor is a high-pitched, harsh sound heard predominantly during inspiration, indicating partial obstruction of the upper airway (larynx, trachea).

================================================================================
Question 663 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Nasopharyngeal carcinoma is treated by:

Options:
  Antibiotics
  Surgery
✓ Radiotherapy
  None of the above
  Chemotherapy

Explanation:
Nasopharyngeal carcinoma (NPC) is highly radiosensitive due to its typical histological features and anatomical location. Therefore, radiotherapy, often combined with chemotherapy, is the primary modality of treatment for NPC, rather than surgery.

================================================================================
Question 664 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Weber’s test in unilateral conductive deafness is lateralized to:

Options:
  The sound ear
✓ The diseased ear
  Both ears
  Zygoma
  Equal on both sides

Explanation:
In unilateral conductive hearing loss, Weber's test (using a tuning fork on the midline of the head) will lateralize to the diseased (affected) ear. This is because bone conduction is better heard in the presence of conductive hearing loss as ambient noise is occluded.

================================================================================
Question 665 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
F.B bronchus is treated by:

Options:
  Eosophagoscopy
  Direct laryngoscopy
  Tonsillectomy
✓ Bronchoscopy
  Indirect laryngoscopy

Explanation:
A foreign body (F.B.) in the bronchus requires removal via bronchoscopy. Bronchoscopy allows for direct visualization of the tracheobronchial tree and retrieval of the foreign object.

================================================================================
Question 666 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Inferior constrictor muscle of the pharynx takes origin from:

Options:
  Hyoid bone
  Mandible
  Maxilla
✓ Thyroid and cricoid cartilages
  Cervical Vertebra

Explanation:
The inferior constrictor muscle of the pharynx originates from the thyroid cartilage and the cricoid cartilage in the larynx.

================================================================================
Question 667 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The pharyngeal pouch passes through:

Options:
  Superior constrictor muscle
✓ Killian dehiscence
  Middle constrictor muscle
  Hyoid bone
  Below inferior Constrictor

Explanation:
A pharyngeal pouch (Zenker's diverticulum) typically herniates through Killian's dehiscence, which is a triangular area of weakness in the posterior pharyngeal wall, located between the cricopharyngeus muscle and the thyropharyngeus part of the inferior constrictor muscle.

================================================================================
Question 668 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The middle ear cleft includes all of the following except:

Options:
  Mastoid air cells
  Middle ear cavity
  Eustachian tube
✓ Vestibular aqueduct
  Attic

Explanation:
The middle ear cleft is a continuous air-filled space comprising the Eustachian tube, middle ear cavity (tympanum), attic (epitympanum), and mastoid air cells. The vestibular aqueduct is a bony canal within the inner ear (vestibular system), not part of the middle ear cleft.

================================================================================
Question 669 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Reactionary bleeding adenoidectomy is treated by:

Options:
✓ Removal of the remnants and post nasal pack
  Antibiotics
  Anterior nasal pack
  Ligation of the bleeding vessel
  Cautery

Explanation:
Reactionary hemorrhage after adenoidectomy typically occurs within the first 24 hours. Management often involves clearing any residual clots, ensuring no adenoid remnants are actively bleeding, and applying a posterior nasal pack (or nasopharyngeal pack) to control the bleeding.

================================================================================
Question 670 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Tonsillectomy is absolutely contraindicated in:

Options:
  Menstruation
  Upper respiratory tract infection
  Quinsy
✓ Bleeding disorders
  Carcinoma Tonsil

Explanation:
Tonsillectomy is absolutely contraindicated in patients with uncorrected bleeding disorders (e.g., hemophilia, severe coagulopathies) due to the high risk of severe and potentially life-threatening hemorrhage.

================================================================================
Question 671 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A patient with epistaxis showing a bleeding point in little’s area is best managed by:

Options:
✓ Cautery
  Anterior nasal pack
  Posterior nasal pack
  Coagulants
  Ligation of Feeding Vessel

Explanation:
Epistaxis originating from Little's area (Kiesselbach's plexus) in the anterior nasal septum is typically amenable to direct pressure and chemical (silver nitrate) or electrical cautery if bleeding persists after initial measures. Cautery directly addresses the bleeding vessel.

================================================================================
Question 672 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Primary atrophic rhinitis characterized by all of the following except:

Options:
  Recurrent epistaxis
  Anosmia
  Bad odor smelled by the neighbors
✓ Affects male only
  Affects females only

Explanation:
Primary atrophic rhinitis (ozena) is characterized by crusting, anosmia, and a foul odor (often smelled by others, not just the patient). It is more common in females and does not affect males only. Option 'd' is therefore the incorrect statement.

================================================================================
Question 673 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Unilateral watery nasal discharge most likely to suggest a diagnosis of:

Options:
  Acute viral rhinitis
✓ CSF rhinorrhea
  Allergic rhinitis
  Rhinoscleroma
  Vasomotor Rhinitis

Explanation:
Unilateral watery nasal discharge, especially if persistent, clear, and increasing with changes in head position or straining, is highly suggestive of cerebrospinal fluid (CSF) rhinorrhea, usually following trauma or surgery to the skull base.

================================================================================
Question 674 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The usual cause of reactionary post tonsillectomy bleeding is:

Options:
✓ Slipped ligature
  Wound infection
  Tonsillar remnant
  Early extubation
  No antibiotic during procedure

Explanation:
Reactionary hemorrhage (bleeding occurring within the first 24 hours post-surgery) after tonsillectomy is most commonly caused by a slipped ligature (suture tie) from a vessel that was initially controlled during the procedure.

Question 675 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
An adult presented with acute onset dysphagia, edema of the uvula and palate, medially pushed tonsil and trismus is most likely to have:

Options:
  Parapharyngeal abscess
  Acute retropharyngeal
✓ Quinsy
  Chronic retropharyngeal abscess
  Ludwigs angina

Explanation:
Acute onset dysphagia, edema of the uvula and palate, a medially pushed tonsil (often with normal morphology), and trismus (difficulty opening mouth) are classic signs of a peritonsillar abscess, commonly known as quinsy.

================================================================================
Question 676 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The following are signs of chronic tonsillitis except:

Options:
  Enlarged cervical lymph nodes
  Inequality of the size of the tonsils
  Pus in the tonsillar crypts
✓ Edema of the uvula
  Flushing of the pillars

Explanation:
Chronic tonsillitis can involve enlarged cervical lymph nodes, asymmetry in tonsil size, and pus in the tonsillar crypts, often with flushing of the pillars. Edema of the uvula is more characteristic of acute severe inflammation, such as in peritonsillar abscess, rather than chronic tonsillitis.

================================================================================
Question 677 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Safe type of chronic suppurative otitis media is characterized by:

Options:
  Scantly offensive ear discharge
✓ Profuse mucopurulent ear discharge
  Marginal perforation
  All of the above
  Blood stained discharge

Explanation:
The 'safe type' of chronic suppurative otitis media (CSOM), also known as tubotympanic CSOM or mucosal CSOM, is characterized by a profuse, mucoid or mucopurulent ear discharge and typically a central perforation of the tympanic membrane. Marginal perforations and offensive, scanty, or blood-stained discharge are more characteristic of the 'unsafe type' (atticoantral/cholesteatomatous CSOM).

================================================================================
Question 678 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The semicircular canals and vestibule are responsible for:

Options:
  Hearing
  Conduction of sound waves
✓ Balance
  Taste
  Smell

Explanation:
The semicircular canals and vestibule (utricle and saccule) are components of the vestibular system within the inner ear, which is primarily responsible for sensing head movement and maintaining balance.

================================================================================
Question 679 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
In unilateral conductive hearing loss, Webber’s test will lateralize to:

Options:
✓ The diseased ear
  The normal ear
  Both ear
  Webber will be normal
  Webber will be Centre

Explanation:
In unilateral conductive hearing loss, Weber's test (tuning fork on the midline of the head) will lateralize to the diseased (affected) ear. This is because the conductive defect blocks out ambient noise, making bone-conducted sound appear louder in the affected ear.

================================================================================
Question 680 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Myringotomy is indicated in:

Options:
  Secretory otitis media
  Acute otitis media with bulging drum
  Otitic barotrauma
✓ All of the above
  For gromette

Explanation:
Myringotomy (surgical incision of the tympanic membrane) is indicated in secretory otitis media (for fluid drainage), acute otitis media with a bulging drum (to relieve pressure and drain pus), and severe otitic barotrauma (to relieve pain and drain blood/fluid). Therefore, it is indicated in all these conditions.

================================================================================
Question 681 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Antro-choanal polyp arises from:

Options:
  Ethmoid sinus
  Sphenoid sinus
✓ Maxillary sinus
  Middle turbinate

Explanation:
An antrochoanal polyp (ACP) is a benign, solitary polyp that originates from the mucosa of the maxillary sinus (antrum) and then grows through the ostium into the nasal cavity and often extends into the choana and nasopharynx.

================================================================================
Question 682 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Unilateral offensive nasal discharge may suspect:

Options:
  Acute rhinitis
  Nasal polyposis
  Epistaxis
✓ Nose F.B
  Magotts Nose

Explanation:
Unilateral offensive nasal discharge, especially in a child, is highly suspicious for a foreign body (F.B.) in the nose. The foreign body causes irritation and often a secondary infection, leading to purulent and foul-smelling discharge.

================================================================================
Question 683 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
One of the predisposing factors for post cricoid carcinoma is:

Options:
✓ Plummer Vinson syndrome
  Vitamin E deficiency
  Vitamin D deficiency
  Chronic tonsillitis
  Carcinoma larynx

Explanation:
Plummer-Vinson syndrome (also known as Paterson-Kelly syndrome), characterized by iron deficiency anemia, dysphagia (due to esophageal webs), and atrophic glossitis, is a well-established predisposing factor for postcricoid carcinoma (a type of hypopharyngeal squamous cell carcinoma).

================================================================================
Question 684 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The most serious complication following adenotonsillectomy is:

Options:
✓ Reactionary hemorrhage
  Respiratory obstruction
  Respiratory infection
  Remnant of Adenoids
  None of the above

Explanation:
The most serious and potentially life-threatening complication following adenotonsillectomy is hemorrhage, which can be primary (within 24 hours, often reactionary) or secondary (after 24 hours, often due to infection).

================================================================================
Question 685 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Trotter’s triad is a clinical diagnosis of:

Options:
  Nasopharyngeal angiofibroma
  Nasopharyngeal cyst
  Petrositis
✓ Nasopharyngeal carcinoma
  Antrochoanal Polyps

Explanation:
Trotter's triad is a clinical complex associated with nasopharyngeal carcinoma, characterized by unilateral conductive deafness (due to Eustachian tube obstruction), trigeminal neuralgia, and ipsilateral soft palate paralysis. This triad helps in the clinical diagnosis of nasopharyngeal carcinoma.

================================================================================
Question 686 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The best treatment of attico-antral disease:

Options:
  Systemetic antibiotics
  Topical antibiotics
✓ Mastoidectomy
  Both topical and systematic antibiotics
  Treated with analgesics only

Explanation:
Attico-antral disease (unsafe type of CSOM) is typically associated with cholesteatoma and bone erosion. The best and definitive treatment for eradicating the disease and preventing complications is surgical mastoidectomy.

================================================================================
Question 687 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The following paranasal sinuses open in the middle meatus except:

Options:
✓ Sphenoid sinus
  Maxillary sinus
  Frontal sinus
  Anterior ethmoid air cells
  Middle ethmoid air cells

Explanation:
The maxillary, frontal, anterior ethmoid, and middle ethmoid sinuses all drain into the middle nasal meatus. The sphenoid sinus drains into the sphenoethmoidal recess, which is superior to the superior nasal meatus.

================================================================================
Question 688 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Posterior nasal packing is indicated in all of the following situations except:

Options:
  Severe posterior epistaxis
✓ Antro-choanal polyp
  Reactionary post-adenoidectomy bleeding
  After removal of nasopharyngeal angiofibroma
  Uncontrolled Epistaxis

Explanation:
Posterior nasal packing is a hemostatic measure used for severe posterior epistaxis, reactionary post-adenoidectomy bleeding, uncontrolled epistaxis, and sometimes after the removal of highly vascular tumors like nasopharyngeal angiofibroma. It is not indicated for an antrochoanal polyp itself, which is typically removed surgically rather than packed.

================================================================================
Question 689 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Quinsy is suppuration in:

Options:
  Parapharyngeal space
✓ Peritonsillar space
  Retropharyngeal space
  Submandibular space
  Submaxillary space

Explanation:
Quinsy is the colloquial term for a peritonsillar abscess, which is a collection of pus in the peritonsillar space, located between the tonsillar capsule and the superior constrictor muscle.

================================================================================
Question 690 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Laryngoscleroma is characterized by:

Options:
✓ Subglottic stenosis
  Vocal cord paralysis
  Mouth ulceration
  Cervical lymph node
  Ca Larynx

Explanation:
Laryngoscleroma, a manifestation of rhinoscleroma (caused by *Klebsiella rhinoscleromatis*), typically affects the upper airway and is characterized by granulomatous inflammation leading to progressive subglottic stenosis, which can cause severe airway obstruction.

================================================================================
Question 691 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Stridor in children can be caused by:

Options:
  Chronic tonsillitis
  Acute rhinitis
  Deviated nasal septum
✓ Inhaled foreign body
  Chronic laryngitis

Explanation:
Stridor (a high-pitched inspiratory sound indicating upper airway obstruction) in children can be caused by various conditions, but an inhaled foreign body is a common and critical cause that requires urgent attention.

================================================================================
Question 692 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Shwartz’s sign may be positive in:

Options:
  Chronic suppurative otitis media
  Atelactatic middle ear
  Meniere’s disease
✓ Otosclerosis
  Accute Suppurative Otitis Media

Explanation:
Schwartze's sign, a reddish blush or 'flamingo pink' appearance of the promontory visible through the tympanic membrane, is a clinical sign that may be positive in early, active otosclerosis, indicating increased vascularity in the otic capsule.

================================================================================
Question 693 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Griessinger’s sign is positive in:

Options:
  Acute petrositis
  Acute sinusitis
  Acute labyrinthitis
✓ Lateral sinus thromophelbitis
  Brain Abscess

Explanation:
Griesinger's sign (edema and tenderness over the mastoid process) is a specific sign associated with lateral sinus thrombophlebitis, a serious intracranial complication of ear infections where the thrombus extends into the mastoid emissary vein.

================================================================================
Question 694 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Recurrent laryngeal nerve is motor to all of the intrinsic muscles of the larynx except:

Options:
  Vocalis muscle
  Posterior cricoarytenoid muscle
  Lateral cricoarytenoid muscle
✓ Cricothyroid muscle
  Interarytenoids

Explanation:
The recurrent laryngeal nerve (RLN) provides motor innervation to all intrinsic muscles of the larynx except the cricothyroid muscle. The cricothyroid muscle is innervated by the external branch of the superior laryngeal nerve.

================================================================================
Question 695 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The only abductor muscle in the larynx is:

Options:
  Sternothyroid muscle
  Lateral cricoaryenoid muscle
  Cricothyroid muscle
✓ Posterior cricoaryenoid muscle
  Vocalis

Explanation:
The posterior cricoarytenoid muscle is the sole abductor muscle of the vocal cords. Its action pulls the vocal cords apart, opening the glottis for breathing.

================================================================================
Question 696 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Secondary post-tonsillectomy bleeding is due to:

Options:
  Incomplete removal
  Foreign body aspiration
✓ Sepsis
  Posterior nasal packing
  Slip of Ligature

Explanation:
Secondary post-tonsillectomy bleeding (bleeding occurring more than 24 hours after surgery, typically 5-10 days) is most commonly due to wound infection (sepsis) in the tonsillar fossa, leading to erosion of blood vessels and hemorrhage.

================================================================================
Question 697 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Pharyngeal diverticulum occurs through:

Options:
  The superior constrictor muscle
  The middle constrictor muscle
✓ The inferior constrictor muscle
  Palatopharyngus muscle
  All of the above

Explanation:
A pharyngeal diverticulum, specifically Zenker's diverticulum (a pulsion diverticulum), occurs through Killian's dehiscence, which is a triangular area of weakness located within the inferior constrictor muscle of the pharynx, between its thyropharyngeal and cricopharyngeal parts.

================================================================================
Question 698 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Cortical mastoidectomy is indicated in:

Options:
  acute mastoiditis not responding to medical treatment
  Bezold’s abscess
  mastoid abscess
✓ all of the above
  Complicated CSOM

Explanation:
Cortical mastoidectomy (Schwartze operation) is indicated in acute mastoiditis not responding to medical treatment, Bezold's abscess (a complication of mastoiditis), and mastoid abscess. Essentially, it's indicated in all acute suppurative mastoid processes that require surgical drainage and eradication of infection.

================================================================================
Question 699 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Stapedectomy is the operation of the choice in:

Options:
  atelactatic middle ear
  Meniere’s disease
✓ otosclerosis
  secretory otitis media
  CSOM

Explanation:
Stapedectomy (or stapedotomy) is the surgical treatment of choice for otosclerosis, a condition where the stapes bone becomes fixed in the oval window, causing conductive hearing loss.

================================================================================
Question 700 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Ear wash is indicated in all of the following except:

Options:
✓ dry central perforation
  wax
  otomycosis
  caloric test
  F.B ear

Explanation:
Ear wash (syringing) is generally contraindicated in the presence of a tympanic membrane perforation, whether central or marginal, as it can introduce water and infection into the middle ear. It is used for wax removal, foreign body removal, and as part of a caloric test.

================================================================================
Question 701 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Facial nerve gives secretomotor supply to:

Options:
  parotid gland
✓ submandibular salivary gland
  pituitary gland
  thyroid gland
  Adrenal gland

Explanation:
The facial nerve (CN VII), via its chorda tympani branch, provides secretomotor innervation to the submandibular and sublingual salivary glands.

================================================================================
Question 702 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Anterior septal perforation may be caused by:

Options:
  polypectomy
  adenoidectomy
  rhinoscleroma
✓ Bilateral cautery for epistaxis
  Nasal packing

Explanation:
Bilateral cautery (especially aggressive or repeated) for epistaxis on the nasal septum can damage the septal mucosa and cartilage on both sides, leading to necrosis and subsequent perforation of the anterior nasal septum.

================================================================================
Question 703 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
All the following are possible complications of acute sinusitis except:

Options:
✓ temporal lobe brain abscess
  cavernous sinus thrombosis
  orbital cellulitis
  osteomylaitis
  Frontal lobe abscess

Explanation:
Acute sinusitis can lead to various complications due to spread of infection. Orbital cellulitis, osteomyelitis (especially frontal bone), frontal lobe abscess, and cavernous sinus thrombosis are all recognized complications. Temporal lobe brain abscess is less common directly from sinusitis; frontal lobe abscess is more typical from frontal sinusitis.

================================================================================
Question 704 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
An infant with bilateral choanal atresia will present by:

Options:
  conductive deafness
  epistaxis
  postnasal discharge
✓ respiratory distress
  Dysphagia

Explanation:
Newborn infants are obligate nasal breathers. Bilateral choanal atresia (blockage of both posterior nasal openings) prevents nasal breathing, leading to severe respiratory distress, particularly when feeding, and is a life-threatening condition.

================================================================================
Question 705 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The immediate management of perforated TM:

Options:
  Antibiotic drops
  Systematic Antibiotics
  Myringo plasty
  Tympanoplasty
✓ Wait and See

Explanation:
For an acute, traumatic tympanic membrane (TM) perforation without signs of infection, the immediate management is typically 'wait and see'. Most small, uncomplicated perforations heal spontaneously within a few weeks to months. Antibiotics are generally not needed unless there's signs of infection.

================================================================================
Question 706 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The following antibiotics are Contraindicated in infectious mononucleosis:

Options:
✓ Ampicilin
  Erythromycin
  Cephalosporin
  Chloramphenicol
  Septran

Explanation:
Ampicillin (and other aminopenicillins like amoxicillin) is contraindicated in infectious mononucleosis because it commonly causes a characteristic widespread maculopapular rash, which is not a true allergic reaction but can be mistaken for one.

================================================================================
Question 707 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
One of the signs of otogenic cerebellar abscess is:

Options:
  hemiplegia
  hemianethesia
  aphasia
✓ dysdiodokokainesia
  Projectile vomiting

Explanation:
Cerebellar abscesses (often otogenic, spreading from middle ear/mastoid infection) present with signs of cerebellar dysfunction, including ataxia, nystagmus, and dysdiadochokinesia (impaired ability to perform rapid alternating movements).

================================================================================
Question 708 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Radical mastoidectomy is indicated in:

Options:
  adhesive otitis media
✓ unsafe type of otitis media with dead ear
  secretory otitis media
  central dry perforation
  Safe type of Otitis media

Explanation:
Radical mastoidectomy is a highly destructive surgical procedure used for extensive, chronic, and complicated cases of 'unsafe type' (atticoantral/cholesteatomatous) otitis media, especially when there is irreversible middle ear damage and profound hearing loss ('dead ear'), aiming to create a dry, safe ear.

================================================================================
Question 709 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Allergic rhinitis is characterized by all the following except:

Options:
  attacks of sneezing
  watery or mucoid rhinorrhea
✓ antrochoanal polyp
  pale or bluish nasal mucosa
  Watering eyes

Explanation:
Allergic rhinitis is characterized by symptoms like sneezing attacks, watery/mucoid rhinorrhea, itchy/watery eyes, and pale or bluish nasal mucosa. While polyps can occur with chronic inflammation, an antrochoanal polyp is a specific type of benign tumor that is not a characteristic feature of allergic rhinitis itself.

================================================================================
Question 710 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Surgical treatment of Meniere’s disease may include:

Options:
  myringoplasty
  ossiculoplasty
  radical mastoidectomy
✓ vestibular nerve section
  Stapedectomy

Explanation:
Meniere's disease is a disorder of the inner ear characterized by episodic vertigo, fluctuating hearing loss, tinnitus, and aural fullness. When medical management fails, surgical options include vestibular nerve section (to eliminate vertigo while preserving hearing), endolymphatic sac decompression, or labyrinthectomy (if hearing is already poor).

================================================================================
Question 711 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Nasopharyngeal angiofibroma is characterized by all the following except:

Options:
✓ lower motor facial nerve paralysis
  recurrent severe epistaxis
  occurs in adolescent boys
  may cause frog face deformity
  Severe Anemia

Explanation:
Juvenile nasopharyngeal angiofibroma (JNA) typically affects adolescent boys, causes recurrent severe epistaxis and nasal obstruction, and can lead to a 'frog face deformity' due to tumor expansion. Severe anemia can result from chronic blood loss. Lower motor facial nerve paralysis is not a characteristic feature of JNA.

================================================================================
Question 712 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The value of functional endoscopic sinus surgery is to:

Options:
  restore sinonasal functions
  preserve sinus drainage through natural ostia
  avoid external scar
✓ all of the above
  None of the above

Explanation:
Functional Endoscopic Sinus Surgery (FESS) aims to restore normal sinonasal function by preserving the natural ostia (drainage pathways) of the sinuses, removing diseased tissue, and improving ventilation. It is performed endoscopically, thus avoiding external scars.

================================================================================
Question 713 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Septal heamtoma is treated by:

Options:
  antibiotics
  antihistaminc
✓ drainage and pack
  septal perforation
  Severe Anemia

Explanation:
A septal hematoma (a collection of blood under the perichondrium of the nasal septum) requires urgent incision and drainage to prevent complications like abscess formation or septal necrosis leading to saddle nose deformity. After drainage, nasal packing is often applied to prevent reaccumulation.

================================================================================
Question 714 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Nasal septal perforation is caused by all the following except:

Options:
  bilateral cautery for epistaxis
✓ allergic rhinitis
  syphilis
  T.B
  Lethal granuloma

Explanation:
Nasal septal perforation can be caused by bilateral cautery for epistaxis, infections like syphilis and tuberculosis, and inflammatory conditions like lethal midline granuloma (now often referred to as NK/T-cell lymphoma). Allergic rhinitis causes inflammation but does not typically lead to septal perforation.

================================================================================
Question 715 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Hump nose is managed by:

Options:
✓ Reduction rhinoplasty
  Augmentation rhinoplasty
  Nasal tip reconstruction
  All of the above
  None of the above

Explanation:
A 'hump nose' (dorsal hump) is typically managed by reduction rhinoplasty, a surgical procedure that involves removing bone and/or cartilage from the nasal dorsum to achieve a straighter profile.

================================================================================
Question 716 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Unilateral nasal obstruction can be the result of the following except:

Options:
  Unilateral choanal atresia
  Antro-choanal polyp
  Marked septal deviation
✓ Septal perforation
  F.B. Nose

Explanation:
Unilateral nasal obstruction can be caused by unilateral choanal atresia, antrochoanal polyp, marked septal deviation, and nasal foreign body. A septal perforation (a hole in the septum) typically causes a whistling sound or crusting, but rarely, if ever, presents as primary nasal obstruction.

================================================================================
Question 717 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Reservoir sign is positive in:

Options:
  Acute petrositis
  Chronic labyrinthitis
  Acute mastoiditis
  Cholesteatoma
✓ CSOM

Explanation:
The 'reservoir sign' refers to the accumulation of mucopurulent discharge in the middle ear cleft, which can be visualized through a perforation in the tympanic membrane. It is characteristic of the 'safe type' of chronic suppurative otitis media (CSOM) or mucosal CSOM.

================================================================================
Question 718 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Rhinoscleroma is treated by the following except:

Options:
  Streptomycin
  Rifampicin
  Radiotherapy
✓ Puncture and lavage
  Chemotherapy

Explanation:
Rhinoscleroma is a chronic granulomatous disease caused by *Klebsiella rhinoscleromatis*. It is primarily treated with long-term antibiotics (e.g., streptomycin, rifampicin, tetracycline). Radiotherapy and sometimes surgery are used for severe cases. Puncture and lavage are not standard treatments for this condition.

================================================================================
Question 719 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Nasopharyngeal angiofibroma is treated by:

Options:
  Antibiotics
  Nasal packing
✓ Surgical excision
  None of the above
  All of the above

Explanation:
Juvenile nasopharyngeal angiofibroma (JNA) is a benign but locally aggressive and highly vascular tumor. The definitive treatment of choice is complete surgical excision, often preceded by embolization to reduce intraoperative bleeding.

================================================================================
Question 720 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The best position after trachestomy:

Options:
  Supine
✓ Semi-sitting
  Standing
  On one side
  Sitting

Explanation:
After a tracheostomy, the patient is usually positioned in a semi-sitting (Fowler's) position. This helps to reduce swelling, promote drainage, facilitate breathing, and prevent aspiration.

================================================================================
Question 721 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Laryngeal lesions are investigated:

Options:
  CT
  MRI
  Endoscopy & Biopsy
✓ All of the above
  None of the above

Explanation:
The investigation of laryngeal lesions typically involves a combination of methods. Endoscopy (flexible or direct laryngoscopy) with biopsy is essential for direct visualization and histological diagnosis. Imaging modalities like CT and MRI are crucial for assessing the extent of the lesion, local invasion, and nodal involvement. Therefore, all of the above are used.

================================================================================
Question 722 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The cause of primary hemorrhage is:

Options:
  Wound sepsis
  Unprepared Patient
  Injury of the pharyngeal muscle
✓ Rising of blood pressure with slipping ligature
  No prophylaxis antibiotics

Explanation:
Primary hemorrhage (bleeding occurring at the time of surgery or immediately post-op, within 24 hours) is often due to inadequate hemostasis (e.g., a vessel not properly ligated or cauterized) compounded by factors like a rise in blood pressure, which can cause a loosely tied ligature to slip.

================================================================================
Question 723 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Fever in diphtheria is:

Options:
  High grade fever
✓ Low grade fever
  Remittent fever
  Intermittent fever
  Rigors and Chills

Explanation:
Diphtheria is characterized by the formation of a pseudomembrane and can cause significant systemic toxicity. However, the fever associated with diphtheria is typically low-grade, despite the severity of the illness.

================================================================================
Question 724 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The causative agent of vincent’s agent:

Options:
✓ Boreli vencent
  Candida albicans
  Barr-epestin virus
  Streptococci
  Staphylococci

Explanation:
Vincent's angina (acute necrotizing ulcerative gingivitis/pharyngitis) is caused by a synergistic infection involving spirochetes (like *Borrelia vincentii*) and fusiform bacteria (*Fusobacterium nucleatum*).

Question 725 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The causative agent of infectious mononucleosis:

Options:
  Boreli vencenti
  Candida albicans
✓ Barr- virus
  Streptococci
  Klebsialla

Explanation:
Infectious mononucleosis (glandular fever) is most commonly caused by the Epstein-Barr virus (EBV), which is sometimes referred to as 'Barr-virus' in some contexts.

Question 726 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
The causative agent of thrush stomatitis is:

Options:
  Boreli vencenti
✓ Candida albicans
  Epestin - Bar virus
  Streptococci
  Klebsialla

Explanation:
Oral thrush (oral candidiasis, or thrush stomatitis) is a fungal infection of the oral mucosa caused by *Candida albicans*.
